Gabapentin is great for synergizing with benzos. If you normally do not feel euphoria from alprozolam and clonazepam, gabapentin will change that.


By itself, the effects are weak. At 1100 mg I experienced noticeable, uplifted mood. Increased talkativeness and a pleasant body vibe.


You could say it had social anxiety cutting effects. Better than my klonopin as it did not make me sleepy.


It's definitely a great "Base" drug if you're experienced with RX drug combinations.

This is like the best stuff for buprenorphine withdrawls ! It's to the point where you can feel the withdrawls start to fade away after you take some... It takes about 3 hours to really kick in... your thought processes get a little more abstract. 


The only complaint is my ability to read is highly affected. 


What is your experience with addiction to gabapentin? I want to make sure I don't get addicted to it. I know its about dose and length of use... 


My rule of thumb is no more than 300 mgs every 4 hours at the most... which works out to 600 every 8 . That small dose is amazing for treating post-opiate withdrawal (PAWS) . I went from not being able to funtion to being able to go back to work in 2 days from neurontin.

I took two 800mg tabs with my daily methadone dose this morning (95MG liquid concentrate) and the buzz was very noticeable and quite enjoyable!  I didn't think that I would like the Gabapentin, but while I was waiting for my bus to go to the clinic to dose this morning I met a young man from boston.  Apparantly Gabapentin is really popular in the new england area and this young man gave me four 800mg tabs to experiment with.  The buzz could be compared to being a little tipsy on alcohol, and it synergized well with the methadone.  I would recommend it to anybody on MMT who wants to enhance their dose a little bit.  This medication is one that you will develop a tolerance to very fast so be careful!

I'm prescribed Lyrica(Pregabalin), which is by far better than Gabapentin in my experience. Both drugs are quite similar though.  I find the best method to get effects is to only take them every 3 days as tolerance ruins it very fast.


       I'm currently on 200mg Pregabalin twice a day. So what I do is save 400mgs a day for 2 days, then on the third day take 1200mgs on an empty stomach first thing in the morning, washed down with a strong coffee and a multivitamin. This may be too strong for some people, but for me its a perfect dose.


       I would strongly advise not taking Gabapentin daily if you want to get good recreational effects from it.

Hi everyone, I hope that I'm not repeating a question that has been asked a bunch of times before in this thread, but I used the search engine and didn't find what I was looking for. So, I have been on gabapentin for anxiety (off label) for about a year now, and I'm ready to quit it completely after my finals. I am getting more and more problems with it, especially with rebound anxiety if I miss a dose, tolerance, and very uncomfortable physical and psychological withdrawal symptoms even when I try to taper down. They are: cold sweats/chills, heart palpitations, paralyzing anxiety, insomnia, depression, fatigue... They go away if I take my dose again/or a higher dose.

<!-- POST END: id=10145124 -->

<!-- POST START: id=10145663 num=286 author=Doomed2pain author_id=202838 date=2011-12-04T19:35:42+0000 -->
### Post #286

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10145663 |
| Author | Doomed2pain |
| Author ID | 202838 |
| Date | Dec 4, 2011 at 7:35 PM |
| Page | 15 |

You need to taper, I was on it for 8 months 3200mg a day for neuropathic pain. Drop 300mg off your dose every week until you're down to 100mg then jump off. That's the best way, it can seriously mess you up if you reduce too slow. I had bad side effects from it anyway, and pregabalin which is a shame as I was hoping it would help my pain but no it turned me into a zombie, made my panic attacks worse, made me shake and affected my coordination, the pregabalin actually made me fall alot of times which caused me to hurt my already injured parts. I got same off low doses as high doses and my body never got used to it. 


Good luck and remember to drop as slow as you can to keep withdrawals to a minimum.

<!-- POST END: id=10145663 -->

Yeah man, gabapentin caused me some of the worst w/d I have ever felt from *anything*, and that says a lot coming from my ex-junkie ass. It was like Suboxone; except it wouldn't end. After a month Sub w/d got significantly better. After a month of gabapentin w/d, it had not eased one bit (take in mind I had been on 2400-3600mg/day for 8 years). I was plagued with agoraphobic anxiety, cold sweats and chills that were as bad as any opioid w/d I'd ever had if not worse, inability to find words and worse short-term memory problems than when I was on it, pretty severe depression, lack of energy, and flu-like muscle pain. Like I said, it wasn't any better after 30 days. I gave in and have been on it since. (I've probably gone into w/d from it ~5 times over the years).

Yes. I find with gabapentin, when taken properly in sequential doses and when you can achieve that great, clear euphoria (sometimes with CEV of moving, watery organic forms), the next day usually has a grand afterglow too. It helps with sleep and when you wake you feel refreshed.


Also, about the psychedelic effects of the drug - they fascinate me. I find once I get to that great glowy place with gabapentin, if I close my eyes it's almost like being able to go inside mini lucid dreams with vivid, spontaneous visuals. I like to lay on my bed and let the visuals happen, sometimes drifting toward sleep, other times remaining relatively conscience and aware.

<!-- POST START: id=10280318 num=293 author=Znegative author_id=152726 date=2012-01-26T17:03:05+0000 -->
### Post #293

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10280318 |
| Author | Znegative |
| Author ID | 152726 |
| Date | Jan 26, 2012 at 5:03 PM |
| Page | 15 |

Yeah gabapentin really does potentiate the body high with opiates, and it's great to use for withdrawal or whenever you're tapering. I'm surprised to hear so many people experience withdrawal from gabapentin. I mean, it makes sense being a gabaergic and all, but I took about 1,200 mg or more a day for half a year and had no problem quitting cold turkey. I guess I'm lucky though.


The thing that pisses me off, is that for some reason, gabapentin has completely lost its recreational value to me. When I first started taking it, a low dose would make me feel speedy, and higher dosages felt like a sloppy Xanax high. Now, if I take any dosage above 600mg, I just feel awful from it. My motor functions become sloppy like I'm drunk, I get a slight body high that feels like the body high from THC, and I become very paranoid and confused. It's so strange that the drug seems to affect me in a COMPLETELY different way now, then it did about a year ago.


In the end though, I can't complain, it's made tapering down on my suboxone so much easier than if I didn't have it. I bet that if I could have a week to hole up in a shitty hotel and detox, I could get by with just the gabapentin and maybe some diphenhydramine.

<!-- POST END: id=10280318 -->

<!-- POST START: id=10324343 num=299 author=TheTwighlight author_id=77655 date=2012-02-11T18:51:31+0000 -->
### Post #299

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10324343 |
| Author | TheTwighlight |
| Author ID | 77655 |
| Date | Feb 11, 2012 at 6:51 PM |
| Page | 15 |

Let me assure everyone here that all at once is the way to go. Then stagger afterwords if you please. Unless you're not looking to get fucked up, because gabapentin will most assuredly fuck your ass up if you dose several grams with little/no tolerance to the drug.


When I first started using the drug about 8 years ago, the highs I experienced was as euphoric and amazing as MDMA, no lie. Different, but the body high...holy shit. Seriously, like 10 hours of straight-up full-body waves of pure ecstasy. The mental high was that of being totally disinhibited, but not to the point where I would wake up the next morning being told shameful stories of the night before, i.e. benzos. Very sociable, energetic even, but still "downered-out", per say. It's very hard to explain. On top of that, there's no comedown and it lasts *all fucking day*.


Downsides are really nothing but some pretty scattered/blurry memories of being high. But most of them are there. Never blacked out on it, that I remember anyway (lol obviously). If taken regularly, like a medication, it most definitely causes some fairly serious short-term memory issues...if you even care. I don't having been a benzo addict for the last decade nearly (I'm 4 months off them now). I don't know what having a good memory even means, so that side effect could be worse. It's not as bad as benzo-memory, so I'm not complaining.


I'm rambling because I'm really high on bupe right now, so I'm gonna go, but I'll be back to check the thread later on. Peace & Love, yoos guys.

<!-- POST END: id=10324343 -->

<!-- POST START: id=10332888 num=304 author=Znegative author_id=152726 date=2012-02-14T22:11:52+0000 -->
### Post #304

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10332888 |
| Author | Znegative |
| Author ID | 152726 |
| Date | Feb 14, 2012 at 10:11 PM |
| Page | 16 |

If you use the search engine, you'll find a gabapentin mega thread that has a lot of helpful information on it.


Gabapentin is not like an SSRI. I believe it is sometimes prescribed as a mood stabilizer, but more often for neurological pain, and for it's anti-seizure capabilities. Like benzodiazepine's (Xanax, clonazepam etc..), Gabapentin works on the same receptors (GABA), though it's kind of unclear as to what it actual does. For anxiety, gabapentin can definately be used. It's not as good as Xanax, clonazepam or diazepam IMO, but it's great for when you don't have access to those drugs. It kicks in after about 20 minutes when taken orally, and last a pretty long time. The one thing about it that sucks, is that once you reach a certain dosage (somewhere around 2 grams I believe), taking more of it will actually decrease how much actually gets absorbed. So the best way to use it for anxiety, I found, is to take it as needed, and if you must take it every day, than keep your dosage low, like 600mg/day.


Hope that helps some.

<!-- POST END: id=10332888 -->

<!-- POST START: id=10455055 num=307 author=bluedom author_id=169925 date=2012-03-27T15:31:48+0100 -->
### Post #307

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10455055 |
| Author | bluedom |
| Author ID | 169925 |
| Date | Mar 27, 2012 at 3:31 PM |
| Page | 16 |

Gabapentin does not work on GABA. It was developed as a GABA analogue but it doesn't seem to work on the same receptors (likewise with pregabalin---it's a total coincidence they actually ended up being among the greatest discoveries by Pharma in recent years)! It's exact mechanism of action is unclear.


[http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabapentin#Pharmacology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gabapentin#Pharmacology)


For me, it takes two hours for gabapentin to kick in. If I drink coke or a carbonated beverage, it takes one hour. 


Gabapentin's bioavailability does decrease with increased dosages, but I believe it's pretty dose dependent meaning that the more you take, the less bioavailable it becomes. 


"Bioavailability for the immediate-release tablets decreases as dose increases; bioavailability is approximately 60%, 47%, 34%, 33%, and 27% following 900, 1,200, 2,400, 3,600, and 4,800 mg/day given in 3 divided doses, respectively. Food has ony a slight effect on rate and extent of absorption (14% increase in AUC and C max ). Bioavailability for the ER tablets is approximately 75% (with food) and 42% to 65% (fasting). T max was 7.3 h (with food) and 5 h (fasting)."


[http://www.drugs.com/ppa/gabapentin.html](https://www.drugs.com/ppa/gabapentin.html)

<!-- POST END: id=10455055 -->

Today, after half a year, I did 3600mg of Gabapentin Neurontin brand. Usually, I would buy Lyrica, but for some reason, I choose Neurontin this time.

Well, In December 2011 I did 24/7 GBL. It was and is to this date, the best drug I have ever did, even if it harms your body or kills you; I know the risks of taking GBL.


In January 2012 I had a nasty WD of GBL. I felt *very* depressed for almost a week. I still think of buying more, but I couldn't.

The point of this story, is that today, after 5 hours of ingesting the pills, I felt **like I was on GBL.** Maybe not so euphoric as I was but... the happiness, the mood lift, the music enhanced, the "warm" feeling.. I don't know the pharmaceutical way of Gabapentin... I don't know how it works, even the prospect of Pfizer says they don't know how it works, but I can assure it feels like a low dose of GBL. It is awesome.


I just wanted to share this. Now I will do some Codeine because I have read it enhances opiates.


I would really like to know how GBL/GHB are connected with Gabapentin...

Just so you realise...


Neurontin is Gabapentin and Lyrica is Pregabalin... Two completely different drugs.


GBL/GHB is a GABAb agonist gabapentin is a GABA analogue.

<!-- POST START: id=10502220 num=315 author=bluedom author_id=169925 date=2012-04-12T03:23:36+0100 -->
### Post #315

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10502220 |
| Author | bluedom |
| Author ID | 169925 |
| Date | Apr 12, 2012 at 3:23 AM |
| Page | 16 |

People have found pregabalin and gapapentin to be highly promiscuous. They are predicted to bind to a ton of human proteins. So the way they exert their activity is through sophisticated network based multitargeting IMO (for now). They're targeting whole systems that regulate your body and this could include the GABA-based systems even though we know they don't bind GABA_A itself directly in vitro. Given the multtargeting nature and natural sequence variability of humans, this is why probably why you see the effect you do and others see a different effect. It is not wholly surprising at all. But I'd argue they are not exerting their activity through GABA directly but rather through other mechanisms. From Wikipedia:


"Gabapentin was initially synthesized to mimic the chemical structure of the neurotransmitter gamma-aminobutyric acid (GABA), but is not believed to act on the same brain receptors. The mechanism of action that leads to its rapid analgesic effect is simply unknown. Some of its activity may involve interaction with voltage-gated calcium channels. Gabapentin binds to the α2δ subunit (1 and 2) and has been found to reduce calcium currents after chronic but not acute application via an effect on trafficking[40] of voltage-dependent calcium channels in the central nervous system.[41] Another possible mechanism of action, reported by Ben Barres and colleagues in Cell in 2009, is that gabapentin halts the formation of new synapses.[42]"


(Hmm, interesting; I didn't know Ben Barres was looking into gabapentin.)

  only downsides of neurontin is that if i take it for more than 3 days in a row, it tends to poop out..plus, when im on neurontin the last thing i would want to do it take some type of test of any sort..lol..my mind is not mush like alcohol but my meory seems impaired..all in all a very good drug..


  have you guys had success using neurontin everyday for months on end??

**SO WOULD I.


****Physical:**

Tardive Dyskenesia/Akathisia

Neuropathy (neck, upper back, feet, and legs burning)

Psychomotor Retardation

Burning Mouth Syndrome (intense)

Bruxism

Tremors/Dysmetria

Muscle Fasiculations

Reduced bowel function

Leg cramping

Dysphagia (frightening)

Ataxia/Physical coordination difficulty

Exhaustion

Intensified craving for cigarettes

Periods of anorexia followed by extreme hunger

Moments of complete shut down

Nausea

Ocular pressure

Eyes burning/itching

Lowered tolerance to stimulus

Sensitivity to light/sound/touch

Burning sensation in left nostril

Chest pain

Difficulty with speech

Reversed reflexes (Plantar)

Headache

Difficulty walking


**Mental:

**PAWS (Post Acute Withdrawal Syndrome)

Mixed episode (wired and tired)

Impaired concentration

Impaired cognitive function

Hypomania (borderline mania at peak effectiveness of drug)

Vegetative state

Moments of complete shut down

Irritability

Aggression

Rage

Lowered tolerance to stimulus of any kind

Feelings of detachment

Uncontrollable crying 

Motivational and Consummatory Anhedonia

Emotional overreaction (high and low)

Sundowning

<!-- POST START: id=10829895 num=333 author=boxednirvana author_id=202119 date=2012-08-16T20:04:29+0100 -->
### Post #333

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10829895 |
| Author | boxednirvana |
| Author ID | 202119 |
| Date | Aug 16, 2012 at 8:04 PM |
| Page | 17 |

I've taken gabapentin recreationally for about two years now.  When I say recreationally I mean once a week at a dose ranging from 1800 mgs to 3600 mgs, taking 300 mgs every 45 minutes until I've completed my dose.  The effects are generally elevated mood, decreased social anxiety, talkativeness, increased feelings of empathy with others, euphoria, slight visual hallucinations, physical energy and ah-may-zing sex.


I've found a few things potentiate it which I haven't seen listed in all 14 pages of this thread.  


Chamomile tea -  When you first start feeling the effects, drink a nice strong cup of the tea (two teabags) or take a ground chamomile capsule.  Definately increases the euphoria and 'downer' effect of gabbies.  


Passionflower tea - basically does the same thing as chamomile tea but with more of a downer effect.


GABA supplements - although they say GABA does not cross the blood/brain barrier, I've found this to be untrue.  Mixed with gabapentin, GABA really amps up the effects.


All the above mixers will cut down on your need to dose high, thus saving precious gabapentin. :D  I notice if I'm doing gabbies with any of them, my dose will can be pretty much cut in half.

<!-- POST END: id=10829895 -->

> Click to expand...
> — spephspeph said:


Its because your body needs to get use to the drug. It needs to get into your system and upping the dose slowly will help keep unwanted side effects away like diarrhea. Also you may be good at 300-600mg. If so let your dr know you don't need to increase it to 900mg and that it is working. 


It's always good to introduce a drug slowly. You never really know how your body will react to a drug. If you have a reaction then it won't be as bad as taking the full amount. I hope this helps.

**Neurontin/gabapentin**


I am curious about this drug. I have been prescribed it in the past, was on a dose of 3200 mgs and am now back on it at 2400 mgs. It is the only drug that works well to manage my anxiety other than benzos which i dont take due to a past addiction. Ive heard it marketed as a 'wonder drug' that helps with depression, anxiety, pain, as well as having some antipsychotic properties and helps with opiate/benzo withdrawls). They market it as being 'non addictive' and safe for use at high doses. This is bullshit as I have become completely dependant on it, and when i go a day without taking it i feel myself getting sick. I went off 3200 mgs in the past and went through withdrawls that i would equate to a mild dope sickness. Also i have taken 4000 mgs and experienced a temporary psychosis. I am just wondering what other peoples experiences are with this drug as it seems to be (in my opinion) as bad as benzoS and i cant grasp why its marketed tge way it is, fucking evil drug companies man... Any ways im just interested to hear what other people think of the drug.

<!-- POST START: id=10855066 num=338 author=ErgicMergic author_id=192487 date=2012-08-28T04:07:50+0100 -->
### Post #338

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10855066 |
| Author | ErgicMergic |
| Author ID | 192487 |
| Date | Aug 28, 2012 at 4:07 AM |
| Page | 17 |

Gabapentin and Pregabalin withdrawal have been likened to a weird mix of an opiate/benzo withdrawal, with a significant amount of mood instability. Gabapentin is *not* a drug I would want to be physically dependent on, especially not on more than 600mg a day.


Your dosage is far too high, which is why you are quite physically dependent. If you require dosages that high, just switch to pregabalin (Lyrica), as it more efficiently crosses the BBB and has a higher BA, making it a more effective anxiolytic and analgesic at lower dosages, cutting down on physical side effects and cognitive impairment.


300mg Gabapentin ~= 100mg Lyrica

<!-- POST END: id=10855066 -->

**Neurontin!**


Hey guys!

I just got prescribed 900mg of neurontin a day, and I find that at 1800mg my anxiety almost completely vanishes.

Also, when I take 1800mg at once I feel a speedy, sensual rush followed by a mellow, less-tired benzoish high.


After years of chronic anxiety, I feel as if I can finally think clearly.

I recommend this drug to anyone who may have anxiety or mild pain... perhaps not as much as a recreational drug.

Also, since I have never been prescribed any "scheduled" or addictive drugs (such as benzos, amphetamines, opiates, ect) it is a relief to find a pill that can finally help with my anxiety, addiction, and depression that is not very dangerous.

Neurontin is almost enough to maker me swear of benzos completely! (I think I might!)


Anyone else have experiences with this wonderful drug?

<!-- POST END: id=10856785 -->

<!-- POST START: id=10856839 num=345 author=ErgicMergic author_id=192487 date=2012-08-28T23:23:31+0100 -->
### Post #345

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10856839 |
| Author | ErgicMergic |
| Author ID | 192487 |
| Date | Aug 28, 2012 at 11:23 PM |
| Page | 18 |

Wait until you go through a week on that high of a dosage, and see if you're still "thinking clearly." Neurontin can cause some serious cognitive impairment at high doses, worse than benzos relative to its anxiolytic potential.


I would recommend using this drug at doses of 600-1200mg at most every other day, or 600mg if you absolutely must take it daily. Short term tolerance builds very quickly with this drug, so it's best to use it no more than 2-3 times a week at a max dosage of 1200-1500mg if you want the full potential.


And, yes, as stated above, use the search engine and welcome to the Bluelight! ![:)](https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/joypixels/assets/8.0/png/unicode/64/1f642.png)

300mg Gabapentin with 200mg L-Theanine down the hatch, for some neuropathic pain relief. I find these two drugs, along with pregabalin, to be amazingly effective for neuropathic pain.

<!-- POST START: id=10909755 num=354 author=ErgicMergic author_id=192487 date=2012-09-18T00:34:32+0100 -->
### Post #354

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 10909755 |
| Author | ErgicMergic |
| Author ID | 192487 |
| Date | Sep 18, 2012 at 12:34 AM |
| Page | 18 |

^ Wow, 3200mg of Gabapentin a day *has* to have horrible cognitive side effects. They don't call it *moron*tin for nothing! ![:)](https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/joypixels/assets/8.0/png/unicode/64/1f642.png)


Also, Gabapentin and Pregabalin greatly potentiates benzos at the cost of "dirtying" up the high and making the making the cognitive side effects of benzos even worse. Be careful with combining the two, as there is much greater potentiation with megadoses of gabapentin/pregabalin mixed with benzos rather than alcohol mixed with benzos. 


Alcohol and benzos are both positive allosoteric modulators of GABA, while gabapentin/pregs actually *increase* the levels of GABA in the brain. Gabapentin is to benzos as gasoline is to fire; you might know the limits of starting a controlled fire, but once you throw some gas on it (gabapentin), things could get messy really quickly.

<!-- POST END: id=10909755 -->

It makes me love everything around me and everything seems interesting.

I find that 6-300mg capsules get me extremely high, like a coke high without the comedown, talkative, happy, on task with household chores ect. Lasts for hours and hours, down side extremely dry mouth but the come down is nice and mellow euphoric until I'm ready for bed.

I can do this about twice a week if I try more tolerance is to high and I just end up sleepy. This was a major help for opiate withdrawal I had a few years back. Also greatly helps with my fibro.

And methadone is a terrible, worthless painkiller.

   But anyhow, my main question is: How strong will the clonazepam end up feeling, dosage-wise?

Since I discontinued it I've suffered horrible symptoms, vision problems, muscle cramps, neuropathy (the pain is the worst I have ever felt, it feels like fire inside me), hypersensitivty, anxiety, insomnia etc etc. I've been bed-ridden for half a year and there is simply no sign of these symptoms ever disappearing. <!-- POST START: id=11125046 num=364 author=TheTwighlight author_id=77655 date=2012-12-12T00:30:06+0000 -->
### Post #364

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 11125046 |
| Author | TheTwighlight |
| Author ID | 77655 |
| Date | Dec 12, 2012 at 12:30 AM |
| Page | 19 |

Toz, although gabapentin is a great drug for many purposes, it causes dependence. I have done every drug under the sun, and been addicted to all kinds of drugs (I used to be a junkie). I have said for a long time, that gabapentin has fucking HORRIBLE withdrawal symptoms that just never seem to end, until I get more of the drug. I have been on either gabapentin or pregabalin (Lyrica) or sometimes both since 2004, and I don't see myself ever getting off them. The withdrawl is like benzodiazepine & opiate withdrawal together. And the higher the dose you're prescribed, the worse it is. I was prescribed OVER the maximum amount that doctors are supposed to prescribe for a long time - 800mg 4x/day (3200mg). It worked for my neuropathy, helped with anxiety, and even helped with depression and bi-polar symptoms. But I have tried to quit several times, and after several days, I was back at the pharmacy in horrible withdrawal anxiously awaiting my refill. It's fucked up.

   So are you saying you were taking 300mg 3 times a day, or 900mg 3 times a day? The way you wrote out your dose is confusing. Either way, you are getting severe symptoms, and you need to go to a doctor and tell him or her what happened. You may need the stuff from this day forward. Or maybe even bring up pregabalin (Lyrica), which is basically gabapentin's big brother, and it works much better. All the best to you, and I hope you get to feeling better. I've been there, man. It sucks.

<!-- POST END: id=11125046 -->

<!-- POST START: id=11128986 num=371 author=Znegative author_id=152726 date=2012-12-13T15:25:01+0000 -->
### Post #371

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 11128986 |
| Author | Znegative |
| Author ID | 152726 |
| Date | Dec 13, 2012 at 3:25 PM |
| Page | 19 |

One thing that I've learned from Gabapentin is that like buprenorphine, in the long run, you're going to be more satisfied with low dosages than high ones.


Wen I was prescribed it initially, I took 300mg in the morning, and 300mg in the evening. I did that for a week, and got a continuous anxiolytic effect with some definate mood-boosting flavor.


However, being the drug pig I was, I decided to start taking higher dosages. While it did get me more fucked up for a few days, I ended up ruining a medication that had been helping me so much. The thing is, it takes no time for tolerance to Gabapentin to develop, but it  takes *forever* for it to go back down. Luckily, I ended up giving up on taking it all together, as doses exceeding 3g's didn't provide more than any dose below that amount. I quit for about two months, and eventually my tolerance went back to baseline, though I unfortunately seemed to have lost all taste for the stuff by then.


For those of you taking such megadoses, remember, the more you take past 1.5 grams, the less is absorbed.

<!-- POST END: id=11128986 -->

> Psychomotor Retardation
> 
> Burning Mouth Syndrome (intense)
> 
> Bruxism
> 
> Tremors/Dysmetria
> 
> Muscle Fasiculations
> 
> Reduced bowel function
> 
> Leg cramping
> 
> Dysphagia (frightening)
> 
> Ataxia/Physical coordination difficulty
> 
> Exhaustion
> 
> Intensified craving for cigarettes
> 
> Periods of anorexia followed by extreme hunger
> 
> Moments of complete shut down
> 
> Nausea
> 
> Ocular pressure
> 
> Eyes burning/itching
> 
> Lowered tolerance to stimulus
> 
> Sensitivity to light/sound/touch
> 
> Burning sensation in left nostril
> 
> Chest pain
> 
> Difficulty with speech
> 
> Reversed reflexes (Plantar)
> 
> Headache
> 
> Difficulty walking
> 
> 
> 
> 
> 
> **Mental:
> 
> **PAWS (Post Acute Withdrawal Syndrome)
> 
> Mixed episode (wired and tired)
> 
> Impaired concentration
> 
> Impaired cognitive function
> 
> Hypomania (borderline mania at peak effectiveness of drug)
> 
> Vegetative state
> 
> Moments of complete shut down
> 
> Irritability
> 
> Aggression
> 
> Rage
> 
> Lowered tolerance to stimulus of any kind
> 
> Feelings of detachment
> 
> Uncontrollable crying

> 
> Emotional overreaction (high and low)
> 
> Sundowning

A week or so... look at the bioavailability of gabapentin with increased doses. It increases rapidly (daily) but also decreases rapidly for me. Even a day's break helps, but a two week break is like restarting from scratch almost. (You will NEVER get the original high again as many an addict knows as long as your brain has a memory of how good that high was---high expectations. ![:)](https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/joypixels/assets/8.0/png/unicode/64/1f642.png)

I'm prescribed 900 mg's 3 times a day (300 mg yellow pills). I usually only take six of 'em though, the doctor just prescribed a high dose so I wouldn't have to worry about refills. I use it for my anxiety and drug cravings and it is excellent. I recently stopped drinking and abusing drugs and have around 50-60 days clean, and this just helps me feel a bit loopy to where I am not on edge every day.


I wanted to say, the bioavailability really doesn't change even if I stagger 300 mgs every 45 minutes or not. If I eat 6 at a time it's just as effective. I think 900 staggered could work better. 


Tolerance to the "high" obviously goes down but it doesn't lose much effectiveness day in and day out. I know, I used to abuse the shit out of this medicine. The big APO GAB 600 mg's. I remember the first time I did some I could hardly walk. Make no mistake, this drug can and will fuck you up if you take enough. Feels really dreamy, almost psychedelic. You feel floaty, and get a sort of weird salivating mouth. I would say it's like alcohol or benzos but it's not. Maybe closer to a barbiturate. It's a wonderful drug, I'd really like to read a study about the long term negative effects. It can make you a bit stupid and you can lose motor coordination pretty easy. But no drug is good for you, truth be told. If anybody has any more information about dose staggering I'd love to hear.

<!-- POST START: id=11502234 num=388 author=AlphaOdure author_id=45607 date=2013-04-20T02:59:12+0100 -->
### Post #388

| Field | Value |

| Page | 20 |

To throw in my $0.02... definitely worthwhile. & i am a former hard drug user (heroin & fentanyl- IV user. 5 yrs clean).


BUT- i am *also* on buprenorphine (subutex formula) & high doses of butalbital (a barbiturate) for back pain.


It DEFINITELY mediates the tolerance and/or feeling of "needing" both buprenorphine & butalbital. But even in 3-4 days of use I am seeing a tolerant effect.


Also, its inconvenient, in that, I must wait till i'm in my controlled environment without any obligations- otherwise i'd appear drunk or at least intoxicated (any slightest hint of me acting/being "different" & my family cries foul & thinks i absolutely MUST be fucking using. Gets pretty annoying after 5 fucking YEARS)... or at the very least, i'd appear without the fullest of my facilities in a work situation.


This is an odd chemical; some of its effects really remind me of baclofen- a GABA-B positive modulator! The psychological state just seems similar; albeit less disorientating, less nauseating, & overall better tolerated. However, unlike baclofen- it does have some hint of adrenergic stimulant effects; particularly w/ sex drive & the mode by which it causes disinhibition- it seems to *not* feel as if it comes from GABAergic action (like ethanol or benzodiazepines); its more stimulatory in its disinhibition. Mind you, its no where near IV'd cocaine. Its important to note also: baclofen HUUGELY reduced my buprenorphine intake inexplicably? Gabapentin has seemed to do this, but, not nearly as rapidly (w/ baclofen- this was around a 50% drop, from 8mg to 4mg in ~2 weeks time w/ absolutely zero discomfort! & i'm a HUUGE pussy when it comes to withdrawal symptoms, too).


**All in all, its a drug that fills certain niches; and for me? A recovering addict on Subutex & butalbital? It works! & i don't "need" my other medications nearly as much.**

<!-- POST END: id=11502234 -->

No, you cannot inject it. IDK why you would anyway. Its necessary for Gabapentin to go through the first pass metabolism stage (I think that's what I read). Sticking it up your bum won't do much good anyway, because of the first pass business.

### Post #392

Its great to see that so many people have wonderful effects from it. I know that as long as I don't use it too frequently, my effects are fantastic. I get a substantial mood lift, massive increase in confidence and sociability, sex drive is fucking *outrageous* with insane erections, sexual performance is increased, but to a natural level (In other words, you can orgasm when you want), energy is off the hook, and music appreciation is increased. A dose lasts about 5 hours or so, and usually takes 1.5-3 hours to start to feel the effects. A common sign of it kicking in is you start getting sleepy. But if you don't fall asleep and keep yourself occupied, it is totally worth it. 


Also, in case my drug use, or lack thereof, comes into question, I will say that I have used *plenty* of drugs, and have been taking in some sort of substance since I was 17; I am now 28. While it hasn't been terribly consistent, I still consider myself a user. I used to be a heavy user, and am now extremely light. I've waterlined heroin, snorted/smoked cocaine, mushrooms, lsd, mdma, gaba, methadone, various opiates/opiods, 4-aco-dmt, pod tea, and others. And of course a myriad of combos. So, having gaba work doesn't always depend on whether a person has used or not. Its the same for Tramadol. Most opiate users can't get off on that stuff. But when I was taking it, I nodded INSANE amounts and for hours. The whole experience lasted 12 hours, if not longer. And I could NOT get off on pod tea, or an inexpensive dose of opiates. BTW, I took over 30 p. somniferum pods last summer. Know what happened? I got the worst case of itchies in the entire history of the human race, for about 6 or so hours. No high, nothing. That should say something. 


Anyway. Gabapentin to date is one of the most simple, yet enjoyable substances. Oh, and getting a solid dose of gaba, smoking bowls, and taking half a melatonin or a muscle relaxer will hammer you. You'll be stoned, have a nice body buzz, but still have energy enough to do stuff. Combos are great.

<!-- POST START: id=11599486 num=394 author=AlphaOdure author_id=45607 date=2013-05-31T13:07:31+0100 -->
### Post #394

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 11599486 |
| Author | AlphaOdure |
| Author ID | 45607 |
| Date | May 31, 2013 at 1:07 PM |
| Page | 20 |

To echo previously stated comments: thank you for posting a thread on gabapentin!


I am on it.. 600mg 4x day (2400mg/day). At first, it was a wonder drug for me; & enjoyable as well. But more importantly- it allowed me to severely drop my daily butalbital intake (a barbiturate), helped w/ anxiety (in an odd.. benzo-ish sort of way), & it created decreased inhibitions, in an odd; stimulatory-sort-of-way (it actually exasperated my sleep issues/insomnia). I had a horny-type feeling reminiscent of cocaine or amphetamine/methamphetamine. It also was a novel and *SUCCESSFUL* antidepressant/mood-stabilizer! As i've tried/have been Rx'd all antidepressants--of all flavors, from tetracyclics to SNRIs; but excluding MAO inhibitors.


*HOWEVER*- after about a week in? These positive effects slowly faded ![:\](https://bluelight.org/xf/BL_Images/Orig_Emoji/wrygrin.gif) They still do, however, potentiate my buprenorphine dose (i take/Rx'd 4mg per day) ONLY if i take it prior to insufflated buprenorphine (it's the Subutex, pill formula).. that's about it, though. No noticeable impact on my butalbital intake (as high as 2000mg/day); antidepressant & mood-stabilizing effects have faded. I planned a quick taper, but, even a moderate reduction (i had ran out for ~4 days) creates extreme anxiety, not entirely unlike moderate withdrawal of butalbital or other barbiturates/GABAergics. So, i'd like to take it slow.. hopefully be able to only use it for situational purposes.


& whoever said (paraphrase) "it causes a high similar to how an antihistamine causes drowsiness" is obviously quite misguided on this medication.

<!-- POST END: id=11599486 -->

benzodiazipines potentiate gabbapentin. this is fact. if u want the gaba potentiated, take the benzos first. if you want the benzos potentiated, take the gaba first but wait 2 hours for your stomach to absorb it or else it will decreas bio availability of the benzo. ever see on a bottle of gabapentin "dont take antacids within 2 hours of taking this medication"?

<!-- POST START: id=11851947 num=406 author=DubiousDoctor author_id=292586 date=2013-09-27T06:57:16+0100 -->
### Post #406

| Post ID | 11851947 |
| Author | DubiousDoctor |
| Author ID | 292586 |
| Date | Sep 27, 2013 at 6:57 AM |
| Page | 21 |

Last I heard the mechanism of action of gabapentin was unknown.  Obviously for pain relief a NSAID would help it.  It is taken up quickly (affecting absorption wouldn't be a big factor) and it is excreted renally so grapefruit juice inhibiting hepatic metoblism via CYP-3A4 wouldn't make a difference.

<!-- POST START: id=11889472 num=410 author=Zwanya author_id=243538 date=2013-10-16T00:01:48+0100 -->
### Post #410

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 11889472 |
| Author | Zwanya |
| Author ID | 243538 |
| Date | Oct 16, 2013 at 12:01 AM |
| Page | 21 |

Gabapentin is excellent for opiate withdrawal, and very soothing with cannabis. I take it as prescribed for chronic pain. The first time I took it (1200mg), along with my medical cannabis, I had strong waves of euphoria for about 2 hours, followed by a very satisfying sleep. Used alone it rid me of any anxiety and offered a mood lift. To echo others, tolerance builds very quickly, so the waves of euphoria turned into decent pain relief soon after my initial experience. 


If you are expecting a narcotic painkiller feel from neurontin, you are going to be disappointed. In my opinion the feeling is utterly different and completely inferior to narcotic painkillers (I used/was prescribed narcotic pain pills for 10 years). The feeling is closer to Ultracet or Ultram, IME. 


I haven't tried Lyrica yet, but I'm looking forward to it as I've heard so many good things about it.

Welcome to Bluelight.

Please don't use Swim. It is against the forum rules and does not help in any way.

Why would you want to take so much DPH to begin with? The deliriant effects at higher doses are very unpleasant and can be dangerous as it lowers the seizure threshold. Or do you have a tolerance to DPH and want to use it for sleep?


Don't know about the combo though but I would avoid the Diphenhydramine. Gabapentin helps great with sleep too.

neurontin was a waste of space & money...IMO

Gabapentin should be taken off the market. The doctor who put me on it when I was detoxing methadone said it was safe and that it worked in GABA ....fucking moron. My current psychiatrist doesn't believe me when I tell him it gives me withdrawals between dosing or that you withdrawal from it period. It's understood that it works in the voltage gated calcium channels containing the α2δ subunit ..... but the lack of understanding exactly how this drug works and the various mechanisms of actions its responsible for resulting in it being prescribed for everything between epilepsy and drug withdrawal is fucking astounding. It's a shit anti-convulsant....its a weak anti-epileptic  ..... it eases nerve pain for fibromyalgia ....yet it lowers the seizure threshold with remeron .... something my doctor decided to add to my regiment wanting to KEEP ME ON gabapentin..... he admitted he recently just discovered that it has recreational value....NO SHIT .....  yet he is hesitant to prescribe me a benzo.  Gabapentin withdrawal is in its own right in-fucking-humane. Mind you I kicked being on methadone for 6 years basically cold turkey with a rapid taper. And this shit is up there with the worst. It's a different type of w/d....with symptoms comparable to opiate/benzo/alcohol all wrapped up in one lovely living hell.


[http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1176314/](http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC1176314/)


GABA B receptor activity.... yet the GABA-B receptor is not completely understood in its ENTIRITY. So its just written off as not having anything to do with it..... this shit is fucking poison. Might as well go sniff a bag of dope....at least heroin/codeine/morphine/alkaloids mechanisms of action are understood and treatable....

<!-- POST END: id=12025379 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12028504 num=432 author=mp3sum author_id=95499 date=2013-12-18T17:27:09+0000 -->
### Post #432

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12028504 |
| Author | mp3sum |
| Author ID | 95499 |
| Date | Dec 18, 2013 at 5:27 PM |
| Page | 22 |

Just found this thread after having been clean off of Lyrica for 6 months. Just wanted to share my experience with those who are just now discovering Pregabalin (Lyrica) and Gabapentin (Neurontin). The former is a much more potent form, perhaps 6x with fewer side effects due to decreased dosage, coupled with a longer half life.


First, I am am a member of the really really enjoy it group. For both I found the body high pleasant, desensitizing, and slightly uncoordinated. Mentally, thinking is slowed, sociability is increased, overall it's quite relaxing.


I started in with Neurontin and progressed to Lyrica back in '05, after discovering it's euphoric effects and then importing a KG of the latter from China. That began a love/hate affair that lasted through July of this year.


Gentlemen, if you fall into my camp and find the effects desirable, PLEASE mind your intake, taking it no more than twice a week or less if to be on the safe side. Lyrica withdrawal is hell, one of the worst I've ever experienced. Prior to this addiction, I ditched both Klonopin and Oxy habits, both per the most common recommendations found on these forums. Yea they sucked, but were ABSOLUTELY doable without the help of others. For Lyrica, rehab was a necessity.


Let me emphasize, that at one of the most famous rehab centers in North America, they had no idea how to deal with Lyrica withdrawal. I received Librium for 1 WEEK, which dear god is just amount the time it takes for one to start fully understanding all that the sudden absence of Lyrica entails. Body and mind are simply short circuited, to the point where one can feel like everything is utterly fucked, shattered, broken. I was depressed, anxious, insomniatic, paranoid, and angry, all of these to the EXTREME. My attending physicians all thought I had several serious mental disorders, and I was actually ejected from the residential program early because they could not handle me. The night I that broke down in tears, I was escorted by security to the Psyche ER. I acted out by throwing some magazines and letting my Psychiatrist know they had no idea how to treat this withdrawal. The next day I was home.


It took about 4 months for me to normalize. During that time my mood and behaviors were erratic. I know taking Neurontin during this time would have eased the pain, but from past experience it would also protract the hellish PAWS. To summarize, understand that you will hurt like all get out. Easily on the same level as benzo/opiate withdrawal, but more of a conflation of the nastiest symptoms. The kicker of course is the duration. A week without Oxy and things subside. A month tapering off benzos and there is noticeable improvement. 3-4 months is what to expect after rocking a serious Lyrica habit, perhaps a month or two with Neurontin due to its shorter half life.


I knew most of this back in 2005, and doctors still do not have a clue. You are the patient, you are the user, so take responsibility and understand the risk associated with abuse of these medications.


/end rant

<!-- POST END: id=12028504 -->

---

| Page | 23 |

Neurontin (gabapentin) and Lyrica (pregabalin) both have a tremendous recreational use history.  In fact, the original generic gabapentin was being used so illicitly that they had to modify it and reintroduce it to the market as brand name Lyrica and make it a controlled substance.

<!-- POST END: id=12042202 -->

This stuff is all fun and games, until you have to stop taking it. I was prescribed it for nuropathy, so I used it as directed everyday at first. Then I decided that getting high was more important that nerve pain, so I started to use it twice a week to keep tolerance down, and potentiated it to hell with codeine, ibuprofen, soda, coffee, nicotine etc depending on the TYPE of gabapentin high I wanted. A week ago, I decided to make a break and get clean, and healthy. So I stopped taking them. And the week that ensured was horrendous! I couldn't sleep, I felt depressed, my body ached, and I was just in a funk all day long. I only managed to get some sleep, after a shot of vodka last night. I'm not a huge drinker so that did help immensely. 


This is just my experience of it. I'm feel a little better today, probably due to getting some sleep. So, be careful with the stuff. I wouldnt say it should be banned, as it is a great pain medication, but using it recreationally can be quite risky.

<!-- POST END: id=12061577 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12071590 num=451 author=Dbear420 author_id=312573 date=2014-01-10T23:24:50+0000 -->
### Post #451

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12071590 |
| Author | Dbear420 |
| Author ID | 312573 |
| Date | Jan 10, 2014 at 11:24 PM |
| Page | 23 |

I was prescribed gabapentin for nerve pain, but found that it was too effective and shut down a whole raft of neural responses, causing loss of sensation throughout the body, severe loss of sensitivity in the sexual sense and absolutely no recreational value whatsoever bar a little drowsiness, and a mild anxyiolitic effect. Now am taking pregabilin, a much superior drug, for anxiety disorders but have not felt much euphoria from it, although I did notice an increase in confidence which is listed in the list of side effects in the patient leaflet, something I greatly needed amongst other things. It's anxyiolitic effects are far greater than gabapentin, but if your gp is exploring this class of drugs for anxiety they will automatically offer gabapentin initially as it is off license and generic versions are cheap, whereas pregabilin is under licence to pfizer who can set the price anywhere they feel like and it means it's about ten times more expensive than gabapentin and all GPs these days have one eye on the budget, so if you have anxiety disorders and get offered gabapentin if I was you I'd do what I did and pressed him to prescribe pregabilin, citing previous use of gabapentin and not tolerating it very well, and am glad I did, pregabilin works quickly and within a couple of days my anxiety levels had become bearable, even comfortable. Do some research and build your argument for being prescribed pregabilin over gabapentin because for anxiety it's head and shoulders above gabapentin.

<!-- POST END: id=12071590 -->

I've never had any wd syndrome from the gabapentin itself...

> — skywatcher63 said:


You mentioned you were also taking Baclofen, which is a strong drug and not one to underestimate. The liver should be checked regularly when using this medication, as mandated by the manufacturer.


You were given two methods already of tracking your meds. 


1. A pillbox 

2. A diary


NO ONE here can tell you whether harm will result if you "accidentally" take extra morphine, Vicodin, Baclofen or Gabapentin. That is a MASSIVE dose of Gabapentin on top of multiple other sedating medications, which you are taking at night. In combination, that is a colossal amount of interacting, sedating medication. 


What we can tell you, is these are highly dangerous drugs on their own, let alone in combination, even more so in older people and with compromised health. People on less substances and in perfect health are found dead in bed, let alone making mistakes and overdosing themselves by failing to manage their medications. This is serious buddy. 


Either use the suggestions to manage the dosing or have someone dispense the meds to you. You won't get someone here making you some kind of arbitrary promise that overdosing on what you are prescribed will be safe and such a promise would be worthless as you should sensibly realise. This is a harm reduction forum. 


Ask your prescribing physician to review these meds and inform them of your concerns so they can help you.

<!-- POST END: id=12151097 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12304855 num=462 author=Lightning-Nl author_id=268399 date=2014-04-28T05:04:41+0100 -->
### Post #462

| Field | Value |

>

> 		
> Click to expand...
> — ad lib said:


Personally, I've found benzo's to be the best for severe nerve pain. I know, I know... benzo's are addictive etc. But seriously, they provide no euphoria (to most people anyways) and I almost never abuse them (I've found them not be psychologically reinforcing at all). Physical addiction is just a side-effect of benzodiazepines. If you take benzo's for more than a couple weeks straight - you will become physically dependent. There is no way around that. However, you will not be psychologically addictive if they are taken correctly.


Anyways, I tried everything for nerve pain. Tons and tons of SSRIS, SNRI's, Channel Blockers (which were the most effective non-controlled substance Rx drugs), antipsychotics and TCA's (both of which just made things a lot worse), and many other drugs. I was prescribed codeine for a small amount of time, but found it be ineffective after any sort of tolerance built up. But benzo's did just the opposite.


I've found that they've made my RLS and nerve pain way better as time has gone on. I no longer suffer RLS during the day, and while I would have RLS at night - the benzo's I'm prescribe for sleep stop that from happening. I no longer have to live my life in physical pain because of exhausted nerves or whatever the fuck causes nerve issues. Also, I've also found benzo tolerance to be no where near what other people have described it to be like.


Maybe that's because I don't abuse my prescriptions? Who knows... All I know is that I've been on Benzo's every day of my life since last August and they're still 90% as effective as they were when I first started taking them.


An exception to the only thing helping for nerve pain (that isn't a benzo) is Nicotine. For some reason, Nicotine has always taken away all of my nerve pain. It's incredibly effective at doing so. I wish doctors would look into this further (explore nAChR as a means of analgesia) because it seems to really work for me...

<!-- POST END: id=12304855 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12304971 num=463 author=Zwanya author_id=243538 date=2014-04-28T07:06:54+0100 -->
### Post #463

Gabapentin worked really well for me for anxiety and pain for the first week or so that I was on it. When mixed with medical cannabis it felt very much like a mild narcotic painkiller.. 


Tolerance developed so quickly that for the rest of my experience with Gabapentin I was trying to recreate what I felt that first week. I was prescribed Gabapentin for about a year. I basically thought of it as ibuprofen, and would take it when I felt particularly anxious. I had a few seizures a month ago and was tapered off of Gabapentin and put on two very strong anti-convulsants. I'm now prescribed Lyrica, and absolutely love it. It is superior to Gabapentin in every way.

| Date | Apr 28, 2014 at 11:32 AM |
| Page | 24 |

> [SwampFox56 said:](https://www.bluelight.org/community/goto/post?id=12304855)
> 
> 
> 
> 			Personally, I've found benzo's to be the best for severe nerve pain. I know, I know... benzo's are addictive etc. But seriously, they provide no euphoria (to most people anyways) and I almost never abuse them (I've found them not be psychologically reinforcing at all). Physical addiction is just a side-effect of benzodiazepines. If you take benzo's for more than a couple weeks straight - you will become physically dependent. There is no way around that. However, you will not be psychologically addictive if they are taken correctly.
> 
> 
> 
> Anyways, I tried everything for nerve pain. Tons and tons of SSRIS, SNRI's, Channel Blockers (which were the most effective non-controlled substance Rx drugs), antipsychotics and TCA's (both of which just made things a lot worse), and many other drugs. I was prescribed codeine for a small amount of time, but found it be ineffective after any sort of tolerance built up. But benzo's did just the opposite.
> 
> 
> 
> I've found that they've made my RLS and nerve pain way better as time has gone on. I no longer suffer RLS during the day, and while I would have RLS at night - the benzo's I'm prescribe for sleep stop that from happening. I no longer have to live my life in physical pain because of exhausted nerves or whatever the fuck causes nerve issues. Also, I've also found benzo tolerance to be no where near what other people have described it to be like.
> 
> 
> 
> Maybe that's because I don't abuse my prescriptions? Who knows... All I know is that I've been on Benzo's every day of my life since last August and they're still 90% as effective as they were when I first started taking them.
> 
> 
> 
> An exception to the only thing helping for nerve pain (that isn't a benzo) is Nicotine. For some reason, Nicotine has always taken away all of my nerve pain. It's incredibly effective at doing so. I wish doctors would look into this further (explore nAChR as a means of analgesia) because it seems to really work for me...
> 		
> Click to expand...
> — SwampFox56 said:


I am rx'ed alprazolam for anxiety, and I do notice that it mildly helps me with my nerve pain. I've been on it for well over 2 years, so I think I'm past the point of worrying about dependency, because I know I am dependent on it. 


I was on oxycodone/apap and hydrocodone/apap for a while. The hydrocodone and apap worked great, but then my doctor decided she no longer wanted to fill that script and then put me on ibuprofen 600mg b.i.d, 100mg Gabapentin and 5mg cyclobenzaprine. I'm also on a SNRI- tried SSRIs with no success. It's quite frustrating that nothing seems to fully help eliminate my pain. Even the Norco didn't fully eliminate it, but it definitely helped more than my current regiment... 


The last time I tried nicotine it triggered my anxiety a bit, but that was a few years ago. I may look into it again. 


> [Zwanya said:](https://www.bluelight.org/community/goto/post?id=12304971)

> 
> 
> 
> Tolerance developed so quickly that for the rest of my experience with Gabapentin I was trying to recreate what I felt that first week. I was prescribed Gabapentin for about a year. I basically thought of it as ibuprofen, and would take it when I felt particularly anxious. I had a few seizures a month ago and was tapered off of Gabapentin and put on two very strong anti-convulsants. I'm now prescribed Lyrica, and absolutely love it. It is superior to Gabapentin in every way.

> — ad lib said:


I was recently switched from Ativan to Klonopin and both have help incredibly well for my nerve pain. I've never tried Xanax to be honest, but the consensus online seems to be that it's one of the better benzo's. Problem is - it's also one of the more addicting benzos and if you start taking it every time you start feeling pain - you could develop a psychological addiction to it.


That's what I did with Ativan (took it every time I started feeling any sort of pain) and while it was INCREDIBLY effective... I had to start taking it more and more often because I would start going into bzd withdrawals... which would give me nerve pain. So they switched me to Klonopin 1 milligram twice a day (just want to point out that's a hell of a dose. Equal to 40 milligrams of Valium a day). But I no longer have nerve pain... like at all... It's been totally eliminated by Klonopin.

> Click to expand...
> — ad lib said:


I personally, got up to 1200 milligrams. Long before that, I told them that Gabapentin was no longer working but they refused to change it. I, personally, experience no side-effects at all from Gabapentin other than horrible rebound insomnia and anxiety when I was 'cold-turkey'd' off of it. Those discontinuation symptoms only lasted for a week, however.


Anyways, have you tried any of the Alpha-agonists? Guanfacine was the only other non-controlled substance that really helped me with nerve pain. You could also look into that (it's trade name is Tenex.) It's usually prescribe for ADHD or Hypertension - but I found it to be very effective for nerve pain when I was on it for ADHD. It did nothing for my ADHD, but it do help a lot with nerve pain.


And yes... good ol' nicotine. Personally, I recommend that you get mentholated cigarettes if you're going to try that. Menthol itself also has some antinociceptive actions and mentholated cigarettes seem to work way better than non-mentholated ones. Also, I have also experienced increased anxiety with non-menthol cigarettes. But menthols were just the opposite - I experienced a very marked reduction in anxiety and much more power painkilling effect.

Would this be good for PAWS depression, instead of screwing with your already screwed up neurotransmitters.

Maybe for short term periods. It's apparent intoxicating effects (not talking nerve pain/seizure indications here) build up tolerance super rapidly. When I took it I'd always feel nice and bit sleepy and energetic. If you try to use it day after day, or any length of time (week+) merely for PAWs, you'll be dependent on gabapentin, and doubly feel shitty.

> 		
> Click to expand...
> — DopeAllah said:


This is a misconception. 


You're body is not 'screwed-up', there are no screwed up neurotransmitters - the neurons in your brain became adapted to having opioids all the time. The body ALWAYS has to keep some sort of homeostasis in order to keep you alive - so the neurons in your brain actually changed to accommodate that opiate use. 


Now that you're body doesn't have to keep itself in homeostasis with the heroin - it will attempt to reach homeostasis once again and eventually you'll feel like you did before your heroin usage.

<!-- POST END: id=12306991 -->

Hey ad lib!


I was on a rather high daily dose--600mg 3 times a day--for anxiety. The side effects were pretty nasty. I gained about 10 pounds; this happened even though I eat local, whole, healthy food, exercise regularly, and do yoga almost daily. My eating/exercising habits never changed, the only element that changed was adding Gabapentin to my meds regimen. 


My skin was also quite irritated on the medication. It would become inflammed often, and I broke out in hives a few times after taking my dose.


If you have any other questions, just shoot me a message. It's no problem at all. ![:)](https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/joypixels/assets/8.0/png/unicode/64/1f642.png)

<!-- POST START: id=12341544 num=480 author=I B Profane author_id=324090 date=2014-05-14T22:51:20+0100 -->
### Post #480

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12341544 |
| Author | I B Profane |
| Author ID | 324090 |
| Date | May 14, 2014 at 10:51 PM |
| Page | 24 |

Not sure if this is the right place to post this...if not, mods please feel free to move it elsewhere where it would be more appropriate ![:)](https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/joypixels/assets/8.0/png/unicode/64/1f642.png)


So I recently got a good amount of these pills that my buddies and I are calling "Gabaprazin." They are pills containing ~400mg of gabapentin and 1-1.5mg of alprazolam.


How is this possible you ask? Well firstly it only works with the gabapentin that comes inside the capsules, I doubt this would work with the big chunky white ones. Butyeah these were made by a friend, who would make them by opening up the cap of gabapentin, dumping a tiiiiny bit of gabapentin powder out and then dropping liquid alprazolam inside the pill, then closing it back up again. The liquid alpraz was inside a PG solution that was worked out to be ~1mg per drop, and when he sold these to me "yeah, if anything these should be fat" (as in, at least 1mg of Xanax in them. I've had sketchy experiences with some pretty weak liquid alpraz and powdered alpraz before so I wanted to make sure I wasn't wasting my money.) I heard the process described, and I guess the gabapentin powder goes from being powdery to chunky and solid once having the 'praz dropped on it, and if you close up the capsule it should stay good and not degrade...


Anyway, I've been experimenting with it a bit as of late. I took one, and expecting the Xanax to kick in right away, was disappointed when I only felt very mild/near placebo effects at the 30 minute mark. I decided to take another and HOLY FUCK it hit me like a freight train, something about the way the pill is set up it takes much longer to feel the alprazolam than just taking a Xanax. Taking a Xanax kicks in quite fast, but with this stuff it takes a lot longer. It's almost like extended release Xanax in a way, with gabapentin to potentiate it. The good news is there is EASILY 1mg or more of alpraz inside these. 1 of these will get me, 2 of these will get me good, and while I've yet to take more than 2 I imagine at that level it would be pretty hard to stay awake. I also take 1-2 mg etizolam on top of these and smoke weed and it gets me feeling quite nice and cozy. And I have a pretty fat downer tolerance FWIW

<!-- POST END: id=12341544 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12345804 num=483 author=mounce author_id=323477 date=2014-05-16T19:07:53+0100 -->
### Post #483

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12345804 |
| Author | mounce |
| Author ID | 323477 |
| Date | May 16, 2014 at 7:07 PM |
| Page | 25 |

I was prescribed gabap for management of phantom limb pain.  Pain wakes me up at night, and my doc said gabap would at least help with that until tolerance builds.  It seemed to reduce spasms consistent with what is reported, and tolerance did build so the sleepiness faded.  For me, I early-on got one ear plugged (doc said no relation) and later a general ringing in my head.  Later, I began to get heart arrhythmia while waiting for sleep (I was taking 600 mg a night), and these symptoms  will clear if I skip a day.  Gabapentin has a half-life of 5-7 hrs.  I was also taking oxycodone once a day, and gabap reduces the effect (so, I wouldn't take oxy *after* gabap).  In any case, on off-days my phantom spasms return.  Doc hoped to reduce oxy Rx, and I am currently trying double-dose gapab one day and oxy the next (effect of oxy seems to improve with its half-life elimination and a 24-hour break- of course a longer break would be better if I could stand it).  Gapap does have a sedating effect that I don't much like in company.  Taken just before bedtime, however, I can depend that it will kick-in and keep me sound asleep until morning.  After effects are a little synthetic compared to the natural feel of an opiate after-effect.

<!-- POST END: id=12345804 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12358207 num=490 author=pinpoint author_id=95916 date=2014-05-22T04:09:14+0100 -->
### Post #490

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12358207 |
| Author | pinpoint |
| Author ID | 95916 |
| Date | May 22, 2014 at 4:09 AM |
| Page | 25 |

Neurontin was a favorite of mine for quite some time. It is like Phenibut's little brother sans the horrible acute withdrawals. Of course there is a withdrawal syndrome associated with Neurontin, but nothing like a full GABA-A/B agonist. I don't trust Pfizer though so I stopped using it. I developed neuropathy (numbness/tingling in the toes) not long after cessation, and although this is anecdotal and quite possibly unrelated it was enough to get me off them. 


The withdrawal is like a mild mix of both a GABA & opiate withdrawal that lasts quite some time. Magnesium helped tremendously (Neurontin is a calcium channel blocker) as well as tapering. 


For those looking to use this drug recreationally you must stagger your doses as only so much can be absorbed and transported across the BBB at a time. 600/mg every hour for 4 hours was enough to get me where I wanted to be without a tolerance. It definitely causes a lack of inhibitions, not so much anxiety, relieves restlessness and is pro-social with a warm subtle euphoria.


Take 600mg 30 minutes after an aleve and continue dosing the Neurontin at that dose for 4 hours.

<!-- POST END: id=12358207 -->

---

> Click to expand...
> — liftedgift said:


Half life doesn't always translate into the subjective effect diminishing to nothing in that time period, or even diminishing by half. Methadone has a 24 hour half life yet people say the analgesic effects last about 12 hours or so. Hydrocodone has a half life of 4-6 hours yet I always felt the stuff for closer to 8-10. It's pretty variable based on your rate of metabolism, and then your expectations on what it *should* feel like.

<!-- POST END: id=12365938 -->

<!-- POST START: id=12370206 num=498 author=pasha author_id=267811 date=2014-05-27T21:08:52+0100 -->
### Post #498

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12370206 |
| Author | pasha |
| Author ID | 267811 |
| Date | May 27, 2014 at 9:08 PM |
| Page | 25 |

> [liftedgift said:](https://www.bluelight.org/community/goto/post?id=12370183)
> 
> 
> 
> 			How exactly does gabapentin work? As far as I can find, it doesn't hit the gaba - b receptor, yet it takes out my phenibut withdrawal.
> 		
> Click to expand...
> — liftedgift said:


gabaergic withdrawal is a mixture of starved gaba receptors and upregulated glutaminergic receptors. it curbs withdrawal by stopping the hyperexcitability of neurons through calcium-channel-blockade. 


------


pregabalin and gabapentin are absolutely horrible with cannabis. i was surprised to see that some people thought it was a great combination in the lyrica megathread.

<!-- POST END: id=12370206 -->

**Gabapentin withdrawal HELL**


I was reading some of the posts about gabapentin withdrawal. I have withdrawn from benzos and SSRI's with much difficulty but I didn't know that getting off of 1800mg of gabapentin would be so horrific. I was on this dose for over 5 years. My new doc wanted me off of it and cut it in half to 300mg three times a day. It has been a month now and I am having tachycardia, extreme agitation, impatience, more hyperactivity than normal. I feel absolutely so beside myself. I am being evaluated for ADHD and my new pdoc won't prescribe low doses of Ritalin because of my higher heart rate so I am also frustrated that I cannot get my cognition under control. I don't remember being so agitated as I am right now. When I went off of a benzo, it was the darkest thoughts of anxiety but withdrawing from gabapentin, I am more emotionally affected. I just picked up some magnesium citrate to see if that will help. I am already on clonazepam 1mg BID. It isn't much help. Any suggestions?

<!-- POST END: id=12393025 -->

no. synergy. not potentiation. it doesn't make it stronger (potentiate) but it acts synergistically (together in harmony) with pregabalin in order to induce a combined effect that can induce greater hypoalgesia than when both substances are taken alone.

<!-- POST START: id=12529146 num=523 author=truncate909 author_id=326913 date=2014-08-13T06:38:52+0100 -->
### Post #523

| Field | Value |
|-------|-------|
| Post ID | 12529146 |
| Author | truncate909 |
| Author ID | 326913 |
| Date | Aug 13, 2014 at 6:38 AM |
| Page | 27 |

Messed about with this recently recreationally, as I had spares. 


Start of the month it took 3000mg, with my prescribed benzos. Just felt like I'd taken a lot more diazepam really, with some visual distortion. Very chatty.


A month later, tried again, this time had to go up to 10000mg for an effect, with my prescribed benzos. This was slightly weird, I was forgetting stuff, doing things 3 or for times, and was just generally out of it. Really not very enjoyable, my tolerance had obviously not come down that much in 4 weeks. Visual distortions more prominent, had to read with one eye like I often need to on Ketamine and opoiates. Reminiscent of that ket RC MXE... Just felt confused and kind of lost in my own house. Didn't enjoy..


I used 1000mg to potentiate 600mg of codeine (also with my prescribed benzos). It didn't do that much really, in the way of positives, but that's subjective. Just felt the nod a lot more with less of the euphoria. Was kind of bored near the end of the peak almost, as with the euphoria being less, my thoughts were quite static.


Drank wine with 6000mg, felt effects noticeably more, but not in a pleasant way. I felt annoyed and a bit confused, and often felt sick. Continued to drink beer after effects had worn off, and felt ok. I guess that's kind of good if you can't afford to buy much booze and have Gabapentin lying about?! But I wouldn't recommend it, especially from a harm reduction standpoint. Not as bad as benzos or opiates with booze I thought though, but I try to avoid drinking on nah those, except my prescribed benzos. 


Also used 900mg for a coke comedown, the coke being imported from the continent and very clean (yellowy/brown stuff). I fell asleep 15 minutes after taking my nightly mirtazapine, with the gabapentin taken an hour prior to that. Doubt it did anything for sleep, as hardly any drugs make me drowsy enough to sleep if my body can fight it now. Fucking benzos! Taper is going well though still, thank god. 


In short, good if you want to potentiate benzos especially if you have a small benzo tolerance, as unlike me you can up your benzo dose, for more effects. That was the equivalent feeling of me taking about 70 to 120mg of Diaz, or a large Xanax dose. Was talking a lot and very happy. With my tolerance that was insane, not felt a benzo type feeling like that one in over a year. That was with 6000mg of GABA and 20mg diazepam. Although I doubt the two drugs will synergies in the same way again like that. I also don't recommend you take similar doses if you are unsure. I was fine, and went out shopping quite happy, you could end up very unstable and slurring. Waking up with bruises, or even in hospital. Don't risk it, you can always take more, never less. Unless you know your own limits then do as you please.


Good for some opiate users I guess, who want to be more sedated. Unsure of it as a comedown drug, although lots swear by it. Due to my tolerance I would have to take a large number of benzos for say an amphetamine comedown, in combination this may help. Although I can't see myself on a meth comedown anytime soon haha. 


This can be a bit weird if you take it medicinally and drink or do recreational drugs, so watch out for that. Nice with weed thlugh!

<!-- POST END: id=12529146 -->

Gabapentin/Neurontin effect's a lot of people differently, I personally love it's effects. I'm around 190/200LB's, and consume anywhere from 12 (3600mg) to 15 (4500mg) of the 300 mg cap's, usually taken on an empty stomach. Effect's begin around 2, or 2 1/2 hour's later, and last around 8 to 10 hours! I feel euphoric, more sociable, creative and just overall damn good, both physically and mentally. Like a mild MDMA/Adderall feeling, without the edge, or the harsh comedown, and also similar to a mild trip at the same time. Tolerance is really the only issue. It build's up FAST. My advise, start with something low and work your way up until you find a dose that work's for you, and I wouldn't worry too much about taking a lot. It's almost impossible to O.D. you have to take a really insane dose for anything fatal to happen. Test have been dome on this, with people consuming up to 49grams! and all recoverd just fine without any additional treatment. Hope this is of any help, have fun and be safe.![8o](https://bluelight.org/xf/BL_Images/Orig_Emoji/eek.gif)

Used Gabapentin to get off methadone, long story short - I ended up taking anywhere between 1800-5000mg up to twice a day. This was last year. After a slow taper im down to 300mg a day and find it difficult to drop any lower... even with the aid of clonazepam. NMDA antagonists like zinc, magnesium and agmatine definitely helped me get this far without a sweat ... sticking to 300 mg until I can re-up on my supplements. I just took the taper reallllllllly slow because I know of the gabapentin withdrawal horror all to well... no thanks.


ALSO cant forget about KRATOM. Tremendous help indeed.

> 
> 
> 			i don't really find this a recreational drug, although some people seem to report some 'recreational' effects when first using. i put recreational in the little '' marks 'cause from what i have read these effects seem to be just drowsiness similar to things like low doses of anti-histamines, not any real euphoria or high. however everyone is different and different people enjoy different things, and please correct me if you are experiencing other effects from this drug. one thing i have heard repeatedly though is that any effects from it go quickly from regular use, so tolerance to them builds up quickly (regarding any 'recreational' effects, not medicinal ones), and people have reported not getting and of these effects after only a short period of regular use even at high raised doses.

**Gabapentin**


Gabapentin is one of the hardest meds I have had to get off of. I was maxed out at 300mg X 6a day. I was put on this in the beginning on 2011 for severe nerve damage to my right foot. Well after 13 surgeries and still having nerve problems I decided to stop taking this as it wasn't helping with the pins and needles or constant burning sensation . Well it’s been a rough road and after allmost 3 weeks I still feel weird. Hot flashes, dizzy, eyes are sensitive to light and very moody (depressed). I mean this crap is not supposed to act like this. I was told this is not going to cause any problems while on or stopping this med. Is there anything I can do to get past this messed up feeling? Does anyone know how long this crap will last? What does this drug do the brain? I have quit taking many drugs including ssri and never had these feelings I have. Some days I feel good and then some days it’s like I want to find a hole and just die in it. I am a very strong minded person and have all ways been able to get past these weird feelings it’s just that every day is different!! Is there anything I can get from one of my many doctors to help with this? I live in Texas so weed is not a legal option. It does help though just wish I could get medical weed. Has anyone had these problems with gaba? I am at my wits end with all of this any help would be greatly appreciated..

Forgot to mention, you should titrate down slowly to avoid the withdraw. Tell your doc that you want to stop so he/she can give lower dose capsules, or they could try you on Lyrica and that would end the withdraw since they are similar and may actually help the pain.

Hello all long time bluelight creeper first time poster. Hopefully this is the best place to put this. I have a legally obtained perscription from my severe frost bite last year. But anyway, i had read the forums and heard mixed reviews about whether or not this could be used recreationally. So heres my night:

10Pm i took 3 300mg pills

11Pm not felling much maybe placebo stimualtion so 3 more 300mg pills

11:30 decied to dive into my 100mg pills and take 10

12Am feeling stimulated no placebo so i take 5 more 300 pills

1Am still stimulated no sedation(which i was looking for) so 10 more 100mg pills

2Am same stimulation 3 more 300 pills

3Am more stimulation so i take 10 more 100mg pills

4Am more stimulation 3 more 300mg pills(at this point i start working out pretty heavilly) 

4:30 5 more 300mg pills and more working out.

5Am im starting to get upset that the effects are not becoming sedative which i thought it would through stagering doses and i had ate snacks between doses or milk.

530 i take my 1mg perscribe klonapin.(i am recovering from a large alprazolam addiction 20mg+ a day so the 1mg is a low dose for me.)

7 am still stimulated tho through the entire night non of the stimulation was anxiety ridden. At this point i take my normal meds i take every night 400mg seraquel, .2mg clonidine, 15mg remron, 100mg vistril. Plus my 6mgs of melatonin. (If you havent guessed im an isomniac) i pop in a movie, get comfy and pass out within the hour.

This is where it gets interesting. I wake up at 12pm and my motor function is gone. Like i drank a 5th of vodka but without nasuea. I stomble around to get my other 1mg of klonapin thinking it was getting fun. I sit down and pass out with the klonapin dissolving in my very cottony mouth. 7Pm i wake up and struggle to read the time on the clock. Fuck moms home in 20minutes and im supposed to have cleaned not to mention be sober (coart ordered) motor function still completely gone i hide everything under my bed and sit down. In the next hour my motor control starts to come back to the point of maybe pulling off sobriety (not really) mom wants to go grocery shopping (fuck) im bumping into walls down the halway and sketchly making it down the stairs and outside to the car without being noticed. Within the next hour my motor coordination went back to almoat completely normal and went on my way home.

I guess the moral of my story start small 'cause this stuff has a very large varriable amount of time to fully kick in.

All in all reminded me of ghb in reverse, stimulation first g'd out 2nd if that makes sense.
